<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">Archie Comics</h1>			<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">
				<div id="siteSub" class="noprint">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>				<div id="contentSub"></div>
				<div id="jump-to-nav"></div>				<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a>
				<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#p-search">Jump to search</a>
				<div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Not to be confused with <a href="/wiki/Archie_(comic_book)" title="Archie (comic book)">Archie (comic book)</a>.</div>

</div></td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Official website</th><td class="url">

<p><b>Archie Comic Publications, Inc.</b> is an <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">American</a> <a href="/wiki/Comic_book" title="Comic book">comic book</a> publisher headquartered in <a href="/wiki/Pelham,_New_York" title="Pelham, New York">Pelham</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_York_(state)" title="New York (state)">New York</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> The company is known for its many titles featuring fictional <a href="/wiki/Adolescence" title="Adolescence">teenagers</a> including <a href="/wiki/Archie_Andrews" title="Archie Andrews">Archie Andrews</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jughead_Jones" title="Jughead Jones">Jughead Jones</a>, <a href="/wiki/Betty_Cooper" title="Betty Cooper">Betty Cooper</a>, <a href="/wiki/Veronica_Lodge" title="Veronica Lodge">Veronica Lodge</a>, <a href="/wiki/Reggie_Mantle" title="Reggie Mantle">Reggie Mantle</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sabrina_Spellman" title="Sabrina Spellman">Sabrina Spellman</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Josie_and_the_Pussycats_(comics)" title="Josie and the Pussycats (comics)">Josie and the Pussycats</a>.
</p><p>The company began in 1939 as <b>MLJ Comics</b>, which primarily published superhero comics. The initial Archie characters (<a href="/wiki/Archie_Andrews" title="Archie Andrews">Archie Andrews</a>, <a href="/wiki/Betty_Cooper" title="Betty Cooper">Betty Cooper</a> and <a href="/wiki/Veronica_Lodge" title="Veronica Lodge">Jughead Jones</a>) were created in 1941 by publisher <a href="/wiki/John_L._Goldwater" title="John L. Goldwater">John L. Goldwater</a> and artist <a href="/wiki/Bob_Montana" title="Bob Montana">Bob Montana</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-VanityFair_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-VanityFair-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> in collaboration with writer Vic Bloom.<sup id="cite_ref-gcd-pep22_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gcd-pep22-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-bl_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bl-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> They first appeared in <i><a href="/wiki/Pep_Comics" title="Pep Comics">Pep Comics</a></i> #22 (<a href="/wiki/Cover-date" class="mw-redirect" title="Cover-date">cover-dated</a> Dec. 1941).<sup id="cite_ref-gcd-pep22_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gcd-pep22-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> With the creation of Archie, publisher John Goldwater hoped to appeal to fans of the <a href="/wiki/Andy_Hardy" title="Andy Hardy">Andy Hardy</a> movies starring <a href="/wiki/Mickey_Rooney" title="Mickey Rooney">Mickey Rooney</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-bl_8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bl-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><i><a href="/wiki/Archie_(comic_book)" title="Archie (comic book)">Archie Comics</a></i> was also the title of the company's longest-running publication, the first issue appearing with a cover date of Winter 1942. Starting with issue #114, the title was shortened to simply <i>Archie.</i> The flagship series was relaunched from issue #1 in July 2015 with a new look and design suited for a new generation of readers.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> Archie Comics characters and concepts have also appeared in numerous films, television programs, cartoons, and video games.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Archie_Comics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="MLJ_Magazines">MLJ Magazines</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Archie_Comics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: MLJ Magazines">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span id="1939.E2.80.931946:_Early_years"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1939–1946:_Early_years">1939–1946: Early years</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Archie_Comics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: 1939–1946: Early years">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r856303569">@media all and (max-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .tmulti>.thumbinner{width:100%!important;max-width:none!important}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{float:none!important;max-width:none!important;width:100%!important;text-align:center}}</style><div class="thumb tmulti tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:104px;max-width:104px"><div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:102px;max-width:102px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:PepComics36a.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/PepComics36a.jpg/100px-PepComics36a.jpg" width="100" height="140" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/PepComics36a.jpg/150px-PepComics36a.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/PepComics36a.jpg/200px-PepComics36a.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1095" data-file-height="1533" /></a></div></div><div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:102px;max-width:102px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:PepNumber67.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/PepNumber67.jpg/150px-PepNumber67.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/PepNumber67.jpg/200px-PepNumber67.jpg 2x" data-file-width="961" data-file-height="1377" /></a></div></div><div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:102px;max-width:102px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:GingerNumber1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/GingerNumber1.jpg/100px-GingerNumber1.jpg" width="100" height="141" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/GingerNumber1.jpg/150px-GingerNumber1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/GingerNumber1.jpg/200px-GingerNumber1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="963" data-file-height="1361" /></a></div></div></div></div><p>Maurice Coyne, <a href="/wiki/Louis_Silberkleit" title="Louis Silberkleit">Louis Silberkleit</a>, and <a href="/wiki/John_L._Goldwater" title="John L. Goldwater">John L. Goldwater</a> formed <b>MLJ Magazines</b> and started publishing in November 1939. The company name was derived from the initials of the partners' first names.<sup id="cite_ref-top_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-top-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Coyne served as MLJ's bookkeeper and <a href="/wiki/Chief_Financial_Officer" class="mw-redirect" title="Chief Financial Officer">CFO</a>. Coyne and Silberkleit had been partners in Columbia Publishing, a pulp company that published its last pulp in the late 1950s. Silberkleit had a college degree from <a href="/wiki/St._John%27s_University_(New_York)" class="mw-redirect" title="St. John&#39;s University (New York)">St. John's University</a>, was a licensed and registered pharmacist, and had a law degree from New York Law School. His efforts were focused on the business, printing, separating, distribution and financial ends of the company. John Goldwater served as editor-in-chief. Goldwater was one of the founders of the <a href="/wiki/Comics_Magazine_Association_of_America" class="mw-redirect" title="Comics Magazine Association of America">Comics Magazine Association of America</a>, and he served as its president for 25 years. (The Comics Magazine Association of America is best known to comic fans for its <a href="/wiki/Comics_Code_Authority" title="Comics Code Authority">Comics Code Authority</a>.) Goldwater was also a national commissioner of the <a href="/wiki/Anti-Defamation_League" title="Anti-Defamation League">Anti-Defamation League</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>MLJ's first comic book, published in November 1939, was <i><a href="/wiki/Blue_Ribbon_Comics" title="Blue Ribbon Comics">Blue Ribbon Comics</a></i> with the first half full color and the last half in red and white tints. In January 1940, <i>Pep Comics</i> debuted with the <a href="/wiki/The_Shield_(Archie_Comics)" class="mw-redirect" title="The Shield (Archie Comics)">Shield</a>, the first USA patriotic comic book hero, created by writer and managing editor <a href="/wiki/Harry_Shorten" title="Harry Shorten">Harry Shorten</a> and designed by artist <a href="/wiki/Irv_Novick" title="Irv Novick">Irv Novick</a>. <i><a href="/wiki/Top_Notch_Comics" class="mw-redirect" title="Top Notch Comics">Top Notch Comics</a></i> was launched in December 1941. Until March 1944, the cover feature of Pep was the Shield when Archie took over the cover. The Shield was a forerunner for <a href="/wiki/Joe_Simon" title="Joe Simon">Joe Simon</a>'s and <a href="/wiki/Jack_Kirby" title="Jack Kirby">Jack Kirby</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Captain_America" title="Captain America">Captain America</a>, being published 14 months earlier.<sup id="cite_ref-bl_8-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bl-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-icsh_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-icsh-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Archie_Comics">Archie Comics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Archie_Comics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Archie Comics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span id="1946.E2.80.931990s"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1946–1990s">1946–1990s</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Archie_Comics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: 1946–1990s">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Andy_Hardy" title="Andy Hardy">Andy Hardy</a> movies were an inspiration for Goldwater to have a comic book about a relatable normal person. Teenaged <a href="/wiki/Archie_Andrews_(comics)" class="mw-redirect" title="Archie Andrews (comics)">Archibald "Chick" Andrews</a> debuted with <a href="/wiki/Betty_Cooper" title="Betty Cooper">Betty Cooper</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jughead_Jones" title="Jughead Jones">Jughead Jones</a> in <i>Pep Comics</i> #22 (Dec. 1941), in a story by writer Vic Bloom and artist <a href="/wiki/Bob_Montana" title="Bob Montana">Bob Montana</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-bl_8-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bl-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> Archie soon became MLJ Magazine's headliner, which led to the company changing its name to <b>Archie Comic Publications.</b> Siberkleit and Coyne discontinued Columbia Publications.<sup id="cite_ref-bl_8-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bl-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> In the late 1950s, Archie Publishing launched its "<a href="/wiki/Red_Circle_Comics" class="mw-redirect" title="Red Circle Comics">Archie Adventure Series</a>" line with a new version of the Shield and two new characters.<sup id="cite_ref-top_11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-top-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The February 1962 issue of <a href="/wiki/Harvey_Kurtzman" title="Harvey Kurtzman">Harvey Kurtzman</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Help!_(magazine)" title="Help! (magazine)">Help!</a></i> magazine featured his parody of the Archie characters in its <i><a href="/wiki/Goodman_Beaver" title="Goodman Beaver">Goodman Beaver</a></i> story, "Goodman Goes Playboy", which was illustrated by frequent collaborator <a href="/wiki/Will_Elder" title="Will Elder">Will Elder</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> <i>Help!</i> publisher <a href="/wiki/James_Warren_(publisher)" title="James Warren (publisher)">Jim Warren</a> received a letter on December 6, 1961, accusing <i>Help!</i> of <a href="/wiki/Copyright_infringement" title="Copyright infringement">copyright infringement</a> and demanding removal of the offending issue from newsstands. Warren was unable to <a href="/wiki/Product_recall" title="Product recall">recall</a> the magazine,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarvey20114_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarvey20114-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> but he agreed to settle out of court rather than risk an expensive lawsuit. Warren paid Archie Comics $1000, and ran a note of apology in a subsequent issue of <i>Help!</i><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKitchenBuhle2009204_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKitchenBuhle2009204-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>  The story was reprinted in the book collection <i>Executive Comic Book</i> in 1962, with the artwork modified by Elder to obscure the appearance of the Archie characters. Archie Comics found their appearance still too close to its copyrighted properties, and threatened another lawsuit. Kurtzman and Elder settled out of court by handing over the copyright to the story. Archie Comics held onto the copyright and refused to allow the story to be republished. A request from Denis Kitchen in 1983 to include the story in his <i>Goodman Beaver</i> reprint collection was turned down.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarvey20114_15-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarvey20114-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>  After <i>The Comics Journal</i> co-owner <a href="/wiki/Gary_Groth" title="Gary Groth">Gary Groth</a> discovered that Archie Comics had allowed the copyright on "Goodman Goes Playboy" to expire, he had the story reprinted in <i>The Comics Journal</i> #262 (September 2004),<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarkstein2010Petersen2010249_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarkstein2010Petersen2010249-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> and made it available as a <a href="/wiki/PDF" title="PDF">PDF</a> on the magazine's website.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFrauenfelder2008_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFrauenfelder2008-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In the mid-1960s, during the period fans and historians call the <a href="/wiki/Silver_Age_of_Comic_Books" title="Silver Age of Comic Books">Silver Age of Comic Books</a>, Archie switched its superheroes to a new imprint, "<a href="/wiki/Red_Circle_Comics" class="mw-redirect" title="Red Circle Comics">Mighty Comics</a> Group," with the MLJ heroes done in the campy humor of <a href="/wiki/Batman_(TV_series)" title="Batman (TV series)">the Batman TV show</a>. This imprint ended in 1967.<sup id="cite_ref-top_11-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-top-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In the early 1970s, Archie Enterprises Inc. went <a href="/wiki/Public_company" title="Public company">public</a>. Just over 10 years later, Louis Silberkleit's son Michael and John Goldwater's son Richard returned Archie Comic Publications to private ownership.<sup id="cite_ref-bl_8-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bl-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> Michael Silberkleit served as chairman and co-publisher, while Richard Goldwater served as president and co-publisher.<sup id="cite_ref-wsj2012_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wsj2012-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>  Coyne retired in the 1970s as CFO.<sup id="cite_ref-bl_8-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bl-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In the 1970s and 1980s, <a href="/wiki/Spire_Christian_Comics" title="Spire Christian Comics">Spire Christian Comics</a>, a line of comic books by Fleming H. Revell, obtained license to feature the Archie characters in several of its titles, including <i>Archie's Sonshine,</i> <i>Archie's Roller Coaster,</i> <i>Archie's Family Album,</i> and <i>Archie's Parables.</i> These comics used Archie and his friends to tell stories with strong Christian themes and morals, sometimes incorporating Bible scripture. In at least one instance, the regular characters meet a <a href="/wiki/Jesus_Christ" class="mw-redirect" title="Jesus Christ">Christ-like</a> figure on the beach, and listen as he gently preaches Christian values.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> 
</p><p>Archie launched a short-lived fantasy and horror imprint, <a href="/wiki/Red_Circle_Comics" class="mw-redirect" title="Red Circle Comics">Red Circle Comics</a>, in the 1970s. The company revived that imprint in the 1980s for its brief line of superheroes comics.<sup id="cite_ref-top_11-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-top-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> Later in the 1980s, Archie planned to publish superheroes again with the <a href="/wiki/Mighty_Comics#Spectrum_Comics" class="mw-redirect" title="Mighty Comics">Spectrum Comics</a> imprint, featuring a number of high-profile talents, but it cancelled this attempt before publishing a single issue.<sup id="cite_ref-tcj_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tcj-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Having licensed Archie's MLJ Superheroes in 1991, <a href="/wiki/DC_Comics" title="DC Comics">DC Comics</a> launched its imprint <a href="/wiki/Impact_Comics" title="Impact Comics">Impact Comics</a> with these heroes.<sup id="cite_ref-cbc_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cbc-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-nyt_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nyt-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="2000s">2000s</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Archie_Comics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: 2000s">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>On April 4, 2003, <a href="/wiki/Dad%27s_Garage_Theatre_Company" title="Dad&#39;s Garage Theatre Company">Dad's Garage Theatre Company</a> in <a href="/wiki/Atlanta" title="Atlanta">Atlanta</a> was scheduled to debut a new play by <a href="/wiki/Roberto_Aguirre-Sacasa" title="Roberto Aguirre-Sacasa">Roberto Aguirre-Sacasa</a>, <i>Archie's Weird Fantasy,</i> which depicted Riverdale's most famous resident coming out of the closet and moving to New York. The day before the play was scheduled to open, Archie Comics issued a cease and desist order, threatening litigation if the play proceeded as written. Dad's Garage artistic director Sean Daniels said, "The play was to depict Archie and his pals from Riverdale growing up, coming out and facing censorship. Archie Comics thought if Archie was portrayed as being gay, that would dilute and tarnish his image."<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> It opened a few days later as "Weird Comic Book Fantasy" with the character names changed.<sup id="cite_ref-wcbf_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wcbf-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> In 2014, Aguirre-Sacasa would become Archie's Chief Creative Officer.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Bill_Yoshida" title="Bill Yoshida">Bill Yoshida</a> learned comic book lettering from <a href="/wiki/Ben_Oda" title="Ben Oda">Ben Oda</a> and was hired in 1965 by Archie Comics, where he averaged 75 pages a week for 40 years for an approximate total of 156,000 pages.<sup id="cite_ref-weiland_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-weiland-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Archie Comics sued music duo <a href="/wiki/The_Veronicas" title="The Veronicas">The Veronicas</a> for trademark infringement in 2005 over the band's name, which Archie Comics alleges was taken from the comic book character. Archie Comics and Sire Records (The Veronicas's record label) reached a settlement involving co-promotion.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2008, Archie Publications once again licensed DC Comics its MLJ Super heroes for a DC Universe integrated line, <a href="/wiki/Red_Circle_Comics" class="mw-redirect" title="Red Circle Comics">Red Circle</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-cbc_23-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cbc-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span id="2010.E2.80.93present"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2010–present">2010–present</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Archie_Comics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: 2010–present">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Following Richard Goldwater's death in 2007 and Michael Silberkleit's in 2008, Silberkleit's widow Nancy and Goldwater's half brother Jonathan became co-CEOs in 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-wsj2012_20-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wsj2012-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> Nancy Silberkleit, a former elementary-school art teacher, was given responsibility for scholastic and theater projects, and Jon Goldwater, a former rock/pop music manager, was responsible for running the company's day-to-day publishing and entertainment efforts.<sup id="cite_ref-wsj2012_20-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wsj2012-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> The company sued Silberkleit in July 2011, and Goldwater filed another lawsuit against her in January 2012, alleging she was making bad business decisions and alienating staff; she in turn sued him for defamation.<sup id="cite_ref-wsj2012_20-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wsj2012-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> As of February 2012, <a href="/wiki/New_York_Supreme_Court" title="New York Supreme Court">New York Supreme Court</a> Justice Shirley Kornreich, in <a href="/wiki/Manhattan" title="Manhattan">Manhattan</a>, had fined Silberkleit $500 for violating the court's autumn order temporarily barring her from the company's headquarters, and said the court might appoint a temporary receiver to protect the company's assets.<sup id="cite_ref-wsj2012_20-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wsj2012-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> As of May 2016, these legal proceedings had been resolved.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>Beginning in 2010, the company partnered with <a href="/wiki/Random_House" title="Random House">Random House Publisher Services</a> for its bookstore distribution which included trade paperbacks, original graphic novels and additional book formats. Archie Comics saw its graphic novel and collected edition output increase from 11 book titles that year to 33 in 2012, and 40 in 2013. The company's sales also increased by 410% for books and 1,000% for e-books since 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-pw_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pw-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Beginning in July 2010, the first issue of <i><a href="/wiki/Life_with_Archie#Volume_2_(The_Married_Life)" title="Life with Archie">Life with Archie</a></i> was launched. The series featured two different storylines exploring two possible futures — a world where Archie marries Betty and a world where he marries Veronica. The series also incorporated more contemporary themes including death, marriage woes, same-sex marriage, cancer, financial problems and gun control.<sup id="cite_ref-pastemagazine_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pastemagazine-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Kevin_Keller_(comics)" title="Kevin Keller (comics)">Kevin Keller</a>, Archie Comics' first gay character, debuted in <i>Veronica</i> #202 in September 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> The character was created out of a conversation between Goldwater and longtime Archie Comics writer-artist <a href="/wiki/Dan_Parent" title="Dan Parent">Dan Parent</a> during the company’s first creative summit, about bringing more diversity to Riverdale.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> The issue sold out at the distributor level, prompting Archie Comics for the first time to issue a second edition of a comic.<sup id="cite_ref-comiclist_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-comiclist-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> In June 2011, Keller was featured in his own four-part miniseries.<sup id="cite_ref-newsarama_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-newsarama-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup>  A bimonthly Kevin Keller series launched with writer-artist Parent in early 2012 received a <a href="/wiki/GLAAD" title="GLAAD">GLAAD</a> award for Outstanding Comic Book the following year.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In March 2011, a copy of <i><a href="/wiki/Archie_(comic_book)" title="Archie (comic book)">Archie Comics</a></i> #1, first published in 1942, was sold at auction for $167,300, a record for a non-superhero comic book.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In April 2011, Archie Comics became the first mainstream comic-book publisher to make its entire line available digitally on the same day as the print release.<sup id="cite_ref-wired.com_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wired.com-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> At the <a href="/wiki/New_York_Comic_Con" title="New York Comic Con">New York Comic Con</a> in October 2011, Archie Comics announced that its superheroes would return as an all-digital line under the <a href="/wiki/Red_Circle_Comics" class="mw-redirect" title="Red Circle Comics">Red Circle imprint</a>, a subscription model with back-issue archive access.<sup id="cite_ref-nyt_24-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nyt-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> The imprint started in 2012 with a new <i><a href="/wiki/New_Crusaders" title="New Crusaders">New Crusaders</a></i> series.<sup id="cite_ref-cbc0_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cbc0-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In October 2013, Archie Comics launched its first horror title, <i><a href="/wiki/Afterlife_with_Archie" title="Afterlife with Archie">Afterlife with Archie</a>,</i> depicting Archie and the gang dealing with a zombie apocalypse that begins in their hometown of <a href="/wiki/Riverdale_(Archie_Comics)" title="Riverdale (Archie Comics)">Riverdale</a>. Written by Archie Comics Chief Creative Officer Roberto Aguirre-Sacasa and drawn by artist Francesco Francavilla, <i>Afterlife with Archie</i> was also the first Archie Comics title to be sold exclusively to comic shops and to carry a rating of "Teen+".<sup id="cite_ref-cbc2_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cbc2-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> The series adapted the Archie characters into a world with adult themes and horror tropes including zombies, the occult, demons, and <a href="/wiki/Cthulhu" title="Cthulhu">Cthulhu</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The success of <i>Afterlife with Archie</i> led to a second horror series, <i><a href="/wiki/Chilling_Adventures_of_Sabrina" title="Chilling Adventures of Sabrina">Chilling Adventures of Sabrina</a>,</i> which launched in October 2014 from Aguirre-Sacasa and artist Robert Hack.<sup id="cite_ref-wired.com_37-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wired.com-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ew_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ew-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> <i>Chilling Adventures of Sabrina</i> takes place in the 1960s in the neighboring town of Greendale, and follows a 16-year-old <a href="/wiki/Sabrina_Spellman" title="Sabrina Spellman">Sabrina Spellman</a> as she struggles to balance her responsibilities as a witch-in-training, with her feeling for her boyfriend, Harvey Kinkle.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On April 9, 2014, Archie Comics announced that the adult version of Archie Andrews featured in the <i>Life with Archie</i> series would die in issue #36 (July 2014), which would also be the second-to-last issue.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> Goldwater said Archie's final fate would be the same in both of the possible parallel futures covered by the series.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> This version of Archie was killed saving Senator Kevin Keller from an assassination attempt.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In July 2014, Archie Comics announced that its superhero imprint Red Circle Comics would be rebranded as <a href="/wiki/Dark_Circle_Comics" title="Dark Circle Comics">Dark Circle Comics</a> in 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> The new imprint focuses on self-contained stories featuring the superheroes from the Red Circle library while exploring the crime, horror, and adventure genres. The first wave included the superheroes the Black Hood, the Fox, and the Shield.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> Dark Circle Comics debuted with <i><a href="/wiki/Black_Hood#Greg_Hettinger" title="Black Hood">The Black Hood</a></i> #1 (Feb. 2015) by writer <a href="/wiki/Duane_Swierczynski" title="Duane Swierczynski">Duane Swierczynski</a> and artist <a href="/wiki/Michael_Gaydos" title="Michael Gaydos">Michael Gaydos</a> in February 2015. The a mature-readers title introduced policer officer Gregory Hettinger, the new Black Hood, who struggles with an addiction to painkillers as a result of a shooting outside a school in Philadelphia.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> The launch continued with <i><a href="/wiki/Fox_(comics)#Archie_Comics" title="Fox (comics)">The Fox</a></i> (April 2015), picking up where Red Circle's <i>The Fox</i> series had left. The series was co-written by <a href="/wiki/Dean_Haspiel" title="Dean Haspiel">Dean Haspiel</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mark_Waid" title="Mark Waid">Mark Waid</a> with art by Haspiel.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Shield_(Archie_Comics)#Victoria_Adams" title="Shield (Archie Comics)">The Shield</a></i> #1 (Oct. 2015) from co-writers Chuck Wendig and Adam Christopher and artist Drew Johnson debuted a new, female Shield named Victoria Adams.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Hangman_(Archie_Comics)" title="Hangman (Archie Comics)">The Hangman</a></i> #1 (Nov. 2015) introduced a supernatural horror series from writer Frank Tieri and artist Felix Ruiz about mob hit-man Mike Minetta making a deal with the devil to become the new Hangman after the previous person to wear the mantle ascended to Heaven.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Archie Comics launched a $350,000 <a href="/wiki/Kickstarter" title="Kickstarter">Kickstarter</a> in May 2015 campaign to help the publisher get three additional series out to the public sooner than otherwise: '<i>Life with Kevin</i>, focusing on Kevin Keller, and new <i><a href="/wiki/Jughead_(comic_book)" title="Jughead (comic book)">Jughead</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Betty_and_Veronica_(comic_book)" title="Betty and Veronica (comic book)">Betty and Veronica</a></i> series.<sup id="cite_ref-ew3_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ew3-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> Five days later, Archie Comics cancelled the campaign after critical response. The company stated that the three titles would still be published at a later time.<sup id="cite_ref-hollywoodreporter_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hollywoodreporter-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> 
</p><p>In March 2015, Archie Comics announced that its two delayed horror series would return under a new imprint, <a href="/wiki/Archie_Horror" title="Archie Horror">Archie Horror</a>, with <i>Chilling Adventures of Sabrina</i> #2 and <i>Afterlife with Archie</i> #8 being released in April and May.<sup id="cite_ref-ew2_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ew2-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Flagship_relaunch">Flagship relaunch</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Archie_Comics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Flagship relaunch">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In December 2014, Archie Comics announced that its flagship series <i><a href="/wiki/Archie_(comic_book)" title="Archie (comic book)">Archie</a></i> would relaunch with a new first issue in July 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-comicsalliance_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-comicsalliance-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> The new series would be a modern take on the Archie characters by writer Mark Waid and artist <a href="/wiki/Fiona_Staples" title="Fiona Staples">Fiona Staples</a>, featuring serialized storylines.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> After the first three issues, Annie Wu drew an issue, followed by new regular artist <a href="/wiki/Veronica_Fish" title="Veronica Fish">Veronica Fish</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup>  The new title received IGN's "Best New Comic Series of 2015" award.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The first title in the company's "New Riverdale" universe, <i>Archie</i> was released with a July 2015 cover date and came in at #7 for comic book sales for the month.<sup id="cite_ref-comichron_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-comichron-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> The next title, <i>Jughead</i>, was released in October. In April 2015, Archie Comics announced <i><a href="/wiki/Betty_and_Veronica_(comic_book)" title="Betty and Veronica (comic book)">Betty and Veronica</a></i> which debuted in July 2016. Also announced was <i><a href="/wiki/Kevin_Keller_(comics)" title="Kevin Keller (comics)">Life with Kevin</a></i>, a digital-first mini-series that debuted in June 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-ign_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ign-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Josie_and_the_Pussycats_(comics)" title="Josie and the Pussycats (comics)">Josie and the Pussycats</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Reggie_and_Me" class="mw-redirect" title="Reggie and Me">Reggie and Me</a></i> followed in September and December 2016.
</p><p>In February 2017, Marvel had licensed Archie Comics to publish Marvel Digests collections for the newsstand market starting in November 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Characters">Characters</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Archie_Comics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Characters">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Archie_Comics_characters" title="List of Archie Comics characters">List of Archie Comics characters</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Archie_and_Riverdale">Archie and Riverdale</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Archie_Comics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Archie and Riverdale">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Archie_Andrews" title="Archie Andrews">Archie Andrews</a></div>
<p><i>Archie</i> is set in the fictional small town of Riverdale. The state or even the general location of the town is unspecified.
</p><p>The <i>New York Times</i> postulated that "the cartoonist Bob Montana inked the original likenesses of Archie and his pals and plopped them in an idyllic Midwestern community named Riverdale because Mr. Goldwater, a New Yorker, had fond memories of time spent in <a href="/wiki/Hiawatha,_Kansas" title="Hiawatha, Kansas">Hiawatha, Kansas</a>."<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Superheroes">Superheroes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Archie_Comics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Superheroes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Dark_Circle_Comics" title="Dark Circle Comics">Dark Circle Comics</a></div>
<p>Initially, MLJ started out publishing humor and adventure strips in anthology comic books as was the standard, but quickly added superheroes in their first title's second issue, <i><a href="/wiki/Blue_Ribbon_Comics" title="Blue Ribbon Comics">Blue Ribbon Comics</a></i> #2, with Bob Phantom.<sup id="cite_ref-top_11-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-top-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> In January 1940, <i>Pep Comics</i> debuted featuring the <a href="/wiki/The_Shield_(Archie_Comics)" class="mw-redirect" title="The Shield (Archie Comics)">Shield</a>, America's first patriotic comic book hero, by writer and managing editor <a href="/wiki/Harry_Shorten" title="Harry Shorten">Harry Shorten</a> and artist <a href="/wiki/Irv_Novick" title="Irv Novick">Irv Novick</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-icsh_13-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-icsh-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>  MLJ's Golden Age heroes also included  the <a href="/wiki/Black_Hood" title="Black Hood">Black Hood</a>, who also appeared in pulp magazines<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-icsh0_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-icsh0-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup> and a radio show;<sup id="cite_ref-icsh0_64-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-icsh0-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> and the Wizard, who shared a title with the Shield.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Later revivals of the MLJ superheroes occurred under a number of imprints: Archie Adventure Series, Mighty Comics, <a href="/wiki/Red_Circle_Comics" class="mw-redirect" title="Red Circle Comics">Red Circle Comics</a><sup id="cite_ref-top_11-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-top-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> and one aborted attempt, Spectrum Comics.<sup id="cite_ref-tcj_22-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tcj-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> Archies Publications then licensed them out to <a href="/wiki/DC_Comics" title="DC Comics">DC Comics</a> in the 1990s for <a href="/wiki/Impact_Comics" title="Impact Comics">Impact Comics</a> universe imprint then again in 2008 for a DC Universe integrated Red Circle line.<sup id="cite_ref-cbc_23-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cbc-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-DC_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DC-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Archie's Silver Age relaunch of its superheroes under the Archie Adventure Series imprint and then the Mighty Comics imprint began with a <a href="/wiki/Shield_(Archie_Comics)#Lancelot_Strong" title="Shield (Archie Comics)">new version of the Shield</a> and two new characters the <a href="/wiki/Jaguar_(Archie_Comics)" title="Jaguar (Archie Comics)">Jaguar</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Fly_(Archie_Comics)" title="Fly (Archie Comics)">Fly</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-top_11-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-top-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> In the mid-1960s with the Silver Age of Comics, Archie switched the heroes to a new imprint, "<a href="/wiki/Mighty_Comics" class="mw-redirect" title="Mighty Comics">Mighty Comics</a> Group", with the revival of all the MLJ heroes done as Marvel parodies with "the campy humor of the Batman TV show."<sup id="cite_ref-top_11-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-top-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> This imprint shift soon brought the company its first super hero team book similar to <a href="/wiki/Marvel_Comics" title="Marvel Comics">Marvel</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Avengers_(comics)" title="Avengers (comics)">Avengers</a> with the <a href="/wiki/Mighty_Crusaders" title="Mighty Crusaders">Mighty Crusaders</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-top1_68-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-top1-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> This imprint ended in 1967.<sup id="cite_ref-top_11-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-top-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>With the conversion of Archie's Red Circle Comics from horror to superheroes in the 1980s, the Mighty Crusaders,<sup id="cite_ref-top1_68-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-top1-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> Black Hood, the Comet, the Fly and two version of the Shields had their own titles.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Archie planned to publish superheroes again in the late 1980s with an imprint called <a href="/wiki/Mighty_Comics#Spectrum_Comics" class="mw-redirect" title="Mighty Comics">Spectrum Comics</a>, featuring a number of high-profile talents, including <a href="/wiki/Steve_Englehart" title="Steve Englehart">Steve Englehart</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jim_Valentino" title="Jim Valentino">Jim Valentino</a>, <a href="/wiki/Marv_Wolfman" title="Marv Wolfman">Marv Wolfman</a>, <a href="/wiki/Michael_Bair" title="Michael Bair">Michael Bair</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kelley_Jones" title="Kelley Jones">Kelley Jones</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Rob_Liefeld" title="Rob Liefeld">Rob Liefeld</a>. Planned Spectrum titles included <i><a href="/wiki/Fly_(Archie_Comics)" title="Fly (Archie Comics)">The Fly</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Fox_(comics)" title="Fox (comics)">The Fox</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Hangman_(Archie_Comics)" title="Hangman (Archie Comics)">Hangman</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Jaguar_(Archie_Comics)" title="Jaguar (Archie Comics)">Jaguar</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Terrific_Three" class="mw-redirect" title="Terrific Three">Mister Justice</a></i>, and <i><a href="/wiki/Shield_(Archie_Comics)" title="Shield (Archie Comics)">The Shield</a></i>. Ultimately, Archie cancelled Spectrum Comics before publishing a single issue.<sup id="cite_ref-tcj_22-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tcj-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2012, Archie Comics relaunched its superhero imprint, <a href="/wiki/Dark_Circle_Comics#Digital_imprint_Red_Circle" title="Dark Circle Comics">Red Circle Comics</a>, as an all-digital line under a subscription model with back issues archive access starting with New Crusader.<sup id="cite_ref-nyt_24-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nyt-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-cbc0_38-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cbc0-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2015, Archie Comics rebranded its superhero imprint under the new title, <a href="/wiki/Dark_Circle_Comics" title="Dark Circle Comics">Dark Circle Comics</a>. It was launched in February with <a href="/wiki/Black_Hood" title="Black Hood">The Black Hood</a> followed by the launch of <i><a href="/wiki/Fox_(comics)#Archie_Comics" title="Fox (comics)">The Fox</a></i> in April, while <i><a href="/wiki/Shield_(Archie_Comics)#Victoria_Adams" title="Shield (Archie Comics)">The Shield</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Hangman_(Archie_Comics)" title="Hangman (Archie Comics)">The Hangman</a></i> followed in September and November.
</p>

<h3><span id=".22New_look.22_series"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="&quot;New_look&quot;_series">"New look" series</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Archie_Comics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: &quot;New look&quot; series">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 2007, Archie Comics launched a "new look" series of stories, featuring Archie characters drawn in an updated, less cartoony style similar to the characters' first appearance. There are a total of seven storylines and each one was published as a four-part storyline in a digest series. Also each "new look" story was based on a Riverdale High novel, a series of twelve novels that were published in the 1990s. The only Riverdale High novels that were not adapted into one of these stories are <i>The Trouble With Candy</i>, <i>Rich Girls Don't Have to Worry</i>, <i>Is That Arabella?</i>, <i>Goodbye Millions</i>, and <i>Tour Troubles</i> due to the "new look" series ending in 2010.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Honors_and_awards">Honors and awards</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Archie_Comics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Honors and awards">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/United_States_Postal_Service" title="United States Postal Service">United States Postal Service</a> included Archie in a set of five 44-cent <a href="/wiki/Commemorative_postage_stamps" class="mw-redirect" title="Commemorative postage stamps">commemorative postage stamps</a> on the theme "Sunday Funnies", issued July 16, 2010. The Archie stamp featured Veronica, Archie, and Betty sharing a chocolate <a href="/wiki/Milkshake" title="Milkshake">milkshake</a>. The other stamps depicted characters from the comic strips <i><a href="/wiki/Beetle_Bailey" title="Beetle Bailey">Beetle Bailey</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Calvin_and_Hobbes" title="Calvin and Hobbes">Calvin and Hobbes</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Garfield" title="Garfield">Garfield</a></i>, and <i><a href="/wiki/Dennis_the_Menace_(U.S._comics)" title="Dennis the Menace (U.S. comics)">Dennis the Menace</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Archie_characters_in_other_media">Archie characters in other media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Archie_Comics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Archie characters in other media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_television_series_and_films_based_on_Archie_Comics" title="List of television series and films based on Archie Comics">List of television series and films based on Archie Comics</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Television">Television</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Archie_Comics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Television">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Animation">Animation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Archie_Comics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Animation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In 1968, <a href="/wiki/CBS" title="CBS">CBS</a> began airing episodes of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Archie_Show" title="The Archie Show">The Archie Show</a></i>, a cartoon series produced by <a href="/wiki/Filmation" title="Filmation">Filmation</a>. Although it only lasted for a single season, it aired in reruns for the next decade, and was followed by several spin-off programs, which used segments from this original Archie show and new material. In 1970, Sabrina, the Teenage Witch got <a href="/wiki/Sabrina_the_Teenage_Witch_(1970_TV_series)" title="Sabrina the Teenage Witch (1970 TV series)">her own animated series</a>, also produced by Filmation. In 1970, another Archie property received the <a href="/wiki/Saturday_morning_cartoon" class="mw-redirect" title="Saturday morning cartoon">Saturday morning cartoon</a> treatment: <a href="/wiki/Josie_and_the_Pussycats_(TV_series)" title="Josie and the Pussycats (TV series)"><i>Josie and the Pussycats</i></a>. Unlike Archie and Sabrina, Josie's show was produced by <a href="/wiki/Hanna-Barbera_Productions" class="mw-redirect" title="Hanna-Barbera Productions">Hanna-Barbera Productions</a>, the company behind such animated hits as <i><a href="/wiki/The_Flintstones" title="The Flintstones">The Flintstones</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Jetsons" title="The Jetsons">The Jetsons</a></i>, and <a href="/wiki/Scooby-Doo,_Where_Are_You!" title="Scooby-Doo, Where Are You!"><i>Scooby-Doo, Where Are You?</i></a>. The show was followed by a spin-off, <i>Josie and the Pussycats in Outer Space,</i> in 1972. <i>The Archie Show</i>, <i>Sabrina, the Teenage Witch</i>, <i>Josie and the Pussycats</i>, and several of the spin-off shows including <i>Josie and the Pussycats in Outer Space</i> are currently available on DVD in complete series boxed sets.
</p><p>In 1987, <a href="/wiki/DIC_Entertainment" title="DIC Entertainment">DIC Entertainment</a> produced an NBC <a href="/wiki/Saturday_morning_cartoon" class="mw-redirect" title="Saturday morning cartoon">Saturday morning cartoon</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_Archies" title="The New Archies">The New Archies</a></i>. This children's television cartoon re-imagined the teenage students of Riverdale High School as pre-teens in junior high. Fourteen episodes of the show were produced, which aired during the show's only season in 1987 and were repeated in 1989. A short-lived Archie Comics series was produced bearing the same title and set in the same universe as the animated series. Reruns of the series ran on The Family Channel's Saturday morning lineup from 1991 to 1993, and on Toon Disney from 1998 to 2002. The cast was basically the same, but Dilton Doiley was replaced as the "intellectual" character by an African American named Eugene. Eugene's girlfriend Amani was another addition to the cast. Archie also gained a dog named Red.
</p><p>In 1999, another animated program featuring Archie and his friends was produced by DIC Entertainment. <i><a href="/wiki/Archie%27s_Weird_Mysteries" title="Archie&#39;s Weird Mysteries">Archie's Weird Mysteries</a></i> featured core Archie characters solving mysteries occurring in their hometown of Riverdale. The show ran on the PAX network for a single 40-episode season, and continues to air sporadically in reruns on various other networks. The complete series was released on DVD in 2012. As a companion to the Archie series, DIC also produced <a href="/wiki/Sabrina_the_Animated_Series" class="mw-redirect" title="Sabrina the Animated Series"><i>Sabrina: the Animated Series</i></a>, <i><a href="/wiki/Sabrina%27s_Secret_Life" title="Sabrina&#39;s Secret Life">Sabrina's Secret Life</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Sabrina:_Friends_Forever" title="Sabrina: Friends Forever">Sabrina: Friends Forever</a></i>; the cartoons featured Sabrina and her aunts at a younger age than they were in the comic books. Tie-in comic book titles were produced for all of these series.
</p><p>In 2012, it was announced that <a href="/wiki/MoonScoop" class="mw-redirect" title="MoonScoop">MoonScoop</a> would produce a new Sabrina the Teenage Witch series titled <i><a href="/wiki/Sabrina:_Secrets_of_a_Teenage_Witch" title="Sabrina: Secrets of a Teenage Witch">Sabrina: Secrets of a Teenage Witch</a></i>. It ran for a single 26-episode season on <a href="/wiki/Hub_Network" class="mw-redirect" title="Hub Network">Hub Network</a> from October 2013 until June 2014.
</p><p>In 2013, MoonScoop announced that it will also produce a new Archie animated series titled <i>It's Archie</i> which will feature Archie and friends in junior high.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> The first season was set to feature 52 11-minute episodes.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> However, since its announcement no other information about the series has been released.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Live_action">Live action</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Archie_Comics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Live action">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="1970_special_and_Archie:_To_Riverdale_and_Back_Again">1970 special and <i>Archie: To Riverdale and Back Again</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Archie_Comics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: 1970 special and Archie: To Riverdale and Back Again">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<p>In the early 1970s, a live-action special of Archie and the Archie characters was aired on U.S. television. In 1990, <a href="/wiki/NBC" title="NBC">NBC</a> aired <i><a href="/wiki/Archie:_To_Riverdale_and_Back_Again" title="Archie: To Riverdale and Back Again">Archie: To Riverdale and Back Again</a></i> (titled <i>Archie: Return to Riverdale</i> on video), a TV movie featuring <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Rich_(actor)" title="Christopher Rich (actor)">Christopher Rich</a> as a 30-something Archie Andrews who returns to his hometown for a high school reunion, and reunites with Betty, Veronica, and several other original comic book characters.
</p>
<h5><span id="Sabrina.2C_the_Teenage_Witch"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Sabrina,_the_Teenage_Witch"><i>Sabrina, the Teenage Witch</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Archie_Comics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Sabrina, the Teenage Witch">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sabrina,_the_Teenage_Witch_(1996_TV_series)" class="mw-redirect" title="Sabrina, the Teenage Witch (1996 TV series)">Sabrina, the Teenage Witch (1996 TV series)</a></div>
<p>In 1996, cable network <a href="/wiki/Showtime_(TV_network)" title="Showtime (TV network)">Showtime</a> aired <a href="/wiki/Sabrina_the_Teenage_Witch_(film)" title="Sabrina the Teenage Witch (film)"><i>Sabrina, the Teenage Witch</i></a>, a live-action TV movie starring <a href="/wiki/Melissa_Joan_Hart" title="Melissa Joan Hart">Melissa Joan Hart</a> as Sabrina. The film served as the pilot for a <a href="/wiki/Sabrina,_the_Teenage_Witch_(1996_TV_series)" class="mw-redirect" title="Sabrina, the Teenage Witch (1996 TV series)">TV series</a>, also starring Hart, which began airing in the fall of 1996 on <a href="/wiki/American_Broadcasting_Company" title="American Broadcasting Company">ABC</a>. The sitcom was relatively faithful to the comic book series, and enjoyed a lengthy run until 2003. It is now available in its entirety on DVD, as is the original TV movie.
</p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Riverdale"><i>Riverdale</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Archie_Comics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Riverdale">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Riverdale_(2017_TV_series)" title="Riverdale (2017 TV series)">Riverdale (2017 TV series)</a></div>
<p>By October 2014, <a href="/wiki/Greg_Berlanti" title="Greg Berlanti">Greg Berlanti</a> was developing a drama series for <a href="/wiki/Fox_(network)" class="mw-redirect" title="Fox (network)">Fox</a> titled <i><a href="/wiki/Riverdale_(2017_TV_series)" title="Riverdale (2017 TV series)">Riverdale</a></i> with Berlanti and <a href="/wiki/Sarah_Schechter" title="Sarah Schechter">Sarah Schechter</a> as executive producers through <a href="/wiki/Berlanti_Productions" class="mw-redirect" title="Berlanti Productions">Berlanti Productions</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Roberto_Aguirre-Sacasa" title="Roberto Aguirre-Sacasa">Roberto Aguirre-Sacasa</a> writing the series. It will feature Archie, Betty, Veronica, Jughead, Reggie, Kevin and Josie &amp; the Pussycats.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> In July 2015, the pilot was moved to <a href="/wiki/The_CW" title="The CW">The CW</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> In addition to the series offering a bold, subversive take on the gang, Aguirre-Sacasa has described <i>Riverdale</i> as "Archie meets <i><a href="/wiki/Twin_Peaks" title="Twin Peaks">Twin Peaks</a></i>".<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The pilot was ordered by the network in January 2016 with filming set to begin in the spring.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> In February 2016, Deadline reported that <a href="/wiki/K.J._Apa" class="mw-redirect" title="K.J. Apa">K.J. Apa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lili_Reinhart" title="Lili Reinhart">Lili Reinhart</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cole_Sprouse" title="Cole Sprouse">Cole Sprouse</a>, <a href="/wiki/Camila_Mendes" title="Camila Mendes">Camila Mendes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ashleigh_Murray" title="Ashleigh Murray">Ashleigh Murray</a>, <a href="/wiki/Madelaine_Petsch" title="Madelaine Petsch">Madelaine Petsch</a> and <a href="/wiki/Luke_Perry" title="Luke Perry">Luke Perry</a> had been cast as <a href="/wiki/Archie_Andrews" title="Archie Andrews">Archie Andrews</a>, <a href="/wiki/Betty_Cooper" title="Betty Cooper">Betty Cooper</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jughead_Jones" title="Jughead Jones">Jughead Jones</a>, <a href="/wiki/Veronica_Lodge" title="Veronica Lodge">Veronica Lodge</a>, <a href="/wiki/Josie_McCoy" class="mw-redirect" title="Josie McCoy">Josie McCoy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cheryl_Blossom" title="Cheryl Blossom">Cheryl Blossom</a> and <a href="/wiki/Families_of_Archie%27s_Gang#Fred_Andrews" title="Families of Archie&#39;s Gang">Fred Andrews</a> and in March 2016, <a href="/wiki/Ross_Butler_(actor)" title="Ross Butler (actor)">Ross Butler</a>, Cody Kearsley, Daniel Yang and Casey Cott were cast as <a href="/wiki/Reggie_Mantle" title="Reggie Mantle">Reggie Mantle</a>, <a href="/wiki/Moose_Mason" title="Moose Mason">Moose Mason</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dilton_Doiley" title="Dilton Doiley">Dilton Doiley</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kevin_Keller_(comics)" title="Kevin Keller (comics)">Kevin Keller</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Film">Film</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Archie_Comics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Film">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 2001, <a href="/wiki/Universal_Studios" class="mw-redirect" title="Universal Studios">Universal Studios</a> and <a href="/wiki/Metro-Goldwyn-Mayer" title="Metro-Goldwyn-Mayer">Metro-Goldwyn-Mayer</a> released <i><a href="/wiki/Josie_and_the_Pussycats_(film)" title="Josie and the Pussycats (film)">Josie and the Pussycats</a></i>, based on the <a href="/wiki/Josie_and_the_Pussycats" title="Josie and the Pussycats">comic of the same name</a>.
</p><p>In 2003, <a href="/wiki/Miramax" title="Miramax">Miramax</a> announced that they were working on a Betty and Veronica movie, but the project was cancelled.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2013, <a href="/wiki/Warner_Bros." title="Warner Bros.">Warner Bros.</a> closed a deal for a live-action movie based on the Archie Comics books with <a href="/wiki/Roy_Lee" title="Roy Lee">Roy Lee</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dan_Lin" title="Dan Lin">Dan Lin</a> producing, Jon Goldwater, <a href="/wiki/Krishnan_Menon" title="Krishnan Menon">Krishnan Menon</a> and Jon Silk executive producing, <a href="/wiki/Roberto_Aguirre-Sacasa" title="Roberto Aguirre-Sacasa">Roberto Aguirre-Sacasa</a> writing and <a href="/wiki/Jason_Moore_(director)" title="Jason Moore (director)">Jason Moore</a> has signed on to direct. The film is described as a "high school comedy based on the original line of Archie Comics set in present-day Riverdale".<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup> In an interview with <a href="/wiki/Comic_Book_Resources" title="Comic Book Resources">Comic Book Resources</a>, Aguirre-Sacasa has hinted about doing an <i><a href="/wiki/Afterlife_with_Archie" title="Afterlife with Archie">Afterlife with Archie</a></i> film.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Broadway">Broadway</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Archie_Comics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Broadway">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 2015, Archie Comics announced that they would be bringing Archie, Betty, Veronica, Jughead and the rest of the Riverdale gang to <a href="/wiki/Broadway_theater" class="mw-redirect" title="Broadway theater">Broadway</a> with an all-new musical. <a href="/wiki/Adam_McKay" title="Adam McKay">Adam McKay</a> is set to write the book for the show while <a href="/wiki/Funny_Or_Die" class="mw-redirect" title="Funny Or Die">Funny Or Die</a> will serve as a presenting partner. CEO Jon Goldwater and CCO <a href="/wiki/Roberto_Aguirre-Sacasa" title="Roberto Aguirre-Sacasa">Roberto Aguirre-Sacasa</a> will oversee production. Triptyk Studios packaged the partnership and Tara Smith, B. Swibel and Adam Westbrook will oversee development of the musical for the company. At this time no creative team for the musical has been announced.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Painting">Painting</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Archie_Comics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Painting">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 2014, the Tripoli Gallery in Southampton, New York, displayed a collected of oil paintings by Gordon Stevenson, also known as <a href="/wiki/Baron_Von_Fancy" title="Baron Von Fancy">Baron Von Fancy</a>, featuring Archie Comic characters in adult-oriented scenes.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Official_site">Official site</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Archie_Comics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Official site">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>According to the publisher, the <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://archiecomics.com">official <i>Archie</i> website</a> receives 40&#160;million hits a month.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup> There have been many <i>Archie</i> licensing deals and products.
</p>
